## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. Common relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects, harvesting/immigration, and time-varying (seasonal) environments.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Affine-in-time per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow environmental trend affecting growth rate)
- Exponential-in-time per-capita growth modulation: dP_dt = (c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * P (systematic change in conditions over time)
- Immigration/emigration offset: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (constant net inflow/outflow added to proportional growth)
- Logistic growth (Verhulst) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity with linear density dependence)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ^ c2) (nonlinear crowding effects)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines with log of density)
- Richards-type generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ^ c2) ^ c3 (flexible approach-to-capacity shape)
- Strong Allee effect (cubic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (growth negative below an Allee threshold)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density dependence plus linear removals)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removals independent of population size)
- Ricker-type continuous-time crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (crowding suppresses recruitment multiplicatively)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affecting growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is nearly proportional to P, the per-capita growth rate (dP_dt / P) is approximately constant (density-independent regime).
- A negative quadratic term in P (e.g., -P^2) indicates crowding/competition leading to a stable carrying capacity equilibrium.
- If per-capita growth dP_dt / P decreases approximately linearly with P, a logistic/Verhulst structure is suggested.
- If per-capita growth decreases roughly with log(P), a Gompertz form is indicated (slowing growth over orders of magnitude).
- If growth becomes negative below a positive population threshold, include an Allee factor like (c * P - 1) to represent mate limitation/cooperation effects.
- A nonzero dP_dt at P ≈ 0 implies immigration (positive offset) or background loss (negative offset) independent of density.
- If equilibria shift downward without changing the basic density-dependence shape, include harvesting terms such as -c * P (proportional) or -c (constant-yield).
- Periodic fluctuations in dP_dt at fixed P suggest time-varying coefficients such as sin(c * t + c) multiplying P or the density-dependent term.
- If density dependence appears weak at low P but strong near capacity (or vice versa), use a theta-logistic exponent on P to tune where crowding dominates.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG15)
============================================================
GT: c0*P**c1 + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=0.4866911314650416\,P^{1/3}+0.4866911314650416\,P\,e^{-0.08577402101126279\,t}.
\]
Key structural requirements for any candidate to match GT for all \(t,P\):

1) It must contain a \(P^{1/3}\) term (non-integer power) with **no denominator dependence on \(P\)**.  
2) It must contain a \(P\cdot e^{kt}\) term with \(k=-0.0857...\) (sign can be set via candidate constant) and again **no extra \(P\)-dependent denominator** multiplying it.  
3) It must not introduce rational-in-\(P\) factors like \(\frac{P^2}{aP+b}\), \(\frac{1}{aP+b}\), \(\frac{1}{P}\), etc., unless they can be eliminated globally (which typically requires making the denominator a constant; but then the resulting \(P\)-dependence is polynomial, not \(P^{1/3}\)).

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–7, 9–23, 26–28, 30–31, 33–35, 38, 40–41, 44–47
All of these are built from sums of terms of the form
- \(\dfrac{P^2(\text{const or }e^{c t})}{P c_1 + c_2}\), \(\dfrac{P(\text{const})}{P c_1 + c_2}\), \(\dfrac{\text{const}}{P c_1 + c_2}\),
- sometimes also \(\dfrac{\cdot}{P+c_2}\) or \(\dfrac{c}{P}\),
- plus possibly a free constant term.

Even if you set many coefficients to 0, any remaining nonzero term is **rational in \(P\)** (a ratio of polynomials in \(P\)), possibly times \(e^{c t}\). If you try to remove the \(P\)-dependence in denominators by setting \(c_1=0\), denominators become constants and the expression becomes a combination of **polynomials in \(P\)** (like \(P^2,P,1\)) and \(P^2 e^{ct}\), etc. None of these can equal \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\). Also, if you keep denominators \(aP+b\), you still cannot produce a fractional power \(P^{1/3}\) exactly for all \(P\). Therefore none of these can match the GT.

So: **1–7, 9–23, 26–28, 30–31, 33–35, 38, 40–41, 44–47: no match**.

### Candidate 8
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + \frac{P c_3}{P c_4 + c_5} + \frac{c_6}{P c_4 + c_5}.
\]
This is linear in \(P\) plus rational terms in \(P\) and an exponential-in-\(t\) term linear in \(P\). There is **no way to create \(P^{1/3}\)** from these components. So **no match**.

### Candidate 24
\[
\text{(rational-in-}P\text{ terms)} + c_8 e^{c_5 t} + c_9.
\]
Still only rational/polynomial in \(P\) plus a pure \(t\)-exponential independent of \(P\). Cannot produce \(P^{1/3}\) nor \(P e^{kt}\) simultaneously in the required way. **No match**.

### Candidate 25
\[
P c_0 + P c_1\frac{(P c_2)^{c_3}}{(P c_2)^{c_3}+1} + P c_4 + P^{c_5}c_6 + c_7\log(P c_8+1)+c_9 t.
\]
This does include a power \(P^{c_5}\), so one might set \(c_5=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). However, GT also needs a \(P e^{-kt}\) term. Candidate 25 has **no exponential in \(t\) multiplied by \(P\)**; the only \(t\)-dependence is \(c_9 t\) (linear), which cannot equal \(P e^{-kt}\) for all \(t,P\). Setting \(c_9=0\) removes \(t\) entirely, still not matching. **No match**.

### Candidate 29
\[
P c_0 + P c_1\frac{(P c_2)^{c_3}}{(P c_2)^{c_3}+1} + P^{c_4}c_5 + c_6 t.
\]
Has \(P^{c_4}\) so could make \(P^{1/3}\), but again no \(P e^{kt}\) term; only linear \(t\). **No match**.

### Candidate 32
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + P c_3 + P^{c_4} c_5 e^{c_6 t} + \frac{c_7 t}{P c_8 + c_9}.
\]
This can produce a \(P e^{kt}\) term (via \(P c_1 e^{c_2 t}\) with \(c_2=-0.0857...\)). But the other GT term is \(P^{1/3}\) **without any \(t\)-dependence**. The only fractional power term here is \(P^{c_4} c_5 e^{c_6 t}\), which necessarily carries \(e^{c_6 t}\) unless \(c_6=0\). If set \(c_6=0\), it becomes \(c_5 P^{c_4}\), and we can set \(c_4=1/3\) to match the \(P^{1/3}\) term. However, then we must eliminate extra terms: \(P c_0\) and \(P c_3\) must be zero (set \(c_0=c_3=0\)), and the rational term \(\frac{c_7 t}{P c_8 + c_9}\) must vanish for all \(t,P\) (set \(c_7=0\)). After these settings, candidate 32 reduces to
\[
P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + c_5 P^{1/3},
\]
which matches GT by choosing \(c_1=0.4866911314650416\), \(c_2=-0.08577402101126279\), \(c_5=0.4866911314650416\).  
So **candidate 32 CAN match**.

### Candidate 36
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + P c_3 + P^{c_4} c_5 e^{c_6 t} + \frac{t}{P c_7 + c_8}.
\]
Same logic as candidate 32: set \(c_6=0\), \(c_4=1/3\), \(c_0=c_3=0\), and eliminate the rational term by making its numerator zero—but here numerator is \(t\) with fixed coefficient 1, so it cannot be removed by parameter choice. You could try to make denominator infinite, impossible with finite constants. Thus an unavoidable extra term \(\frac{t}{Pc_7+c_8}\) remains. **No match**.

### Candidate 37
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + \frac{c_3 t}{P + c_4} + \frac{c_5}{P c_6 + c_4}.
\]
No \(P^{1/3}\) term. Also has unavoidable rational terms unless coefficients set to 0, but still no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 39
Contains \(P^{c_1}c_2\) so could make \(P^{1/3}\), but its \(t\)-dependence is via \(\frac{c_3 t}{c_4 t+c_5}\), \(1/(c_4 t+c_5)\), plus an exponential of a rational function of \(P\): \(c_6\exp(c_7/(Pc_8+c_9))\). There is no way to obtain exactly \(P e^{-kt}\) (exponential in \(t\) times \(P\)) from these pieces for all \(t,P\). **No match**.

### Candidate 42
Has \(P^{c_4}c_5\) (can make \(P^{1/3}\)) but its exponential is \(c_6 e^{P c_7}\) (depends on \(P\), not \(t\)), and only linear \(t\) term \(c_8 t\). No \(P e^{-kt}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 43
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + \frac{P c_3}{P c_4 + c_5} + \frac{c_6}{P + c_5}.
\]
No \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 48
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + P^{c_3}c_4 + \frac{c_5 t}{c_6 t+c_7} + \frac{c_8}{c_6 t+c_7} + t.
\]
Can match \(P e^{kt}\) and \(P^{1/3}\) by setting \(c_2=-0.0857...\), \(c_3=1/3\), and coefficients appropriately. But there are unavoidable extra \(t\)-only terms: even if you set \(c_5=c_8=0\), the final “\(+t\)” remains with fixed coefficient 1. So cannot equal GT for all \(t\). **No match**.

### Candidate 49
Has \(P^{c_5}c_6\) (could do \(P^{1/3}\)) but exponential is \(c_7 e^{P c_8}\) (wrong variable), and has \(c_9 t\) not \(P e^{-kt}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 50
\[
P c_0 + P c_1 e^{c_2 t} + \frac{P c_3}{P c_4 + c_5} + \frac{c_6}{P}.
\]
No \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

Conclusion: only candidate **32** can be parameterized to exactly equal the GT.

GT: c0*P**c1 + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: [32]
Matched candidates: ["P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3 + P**c4*c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*t/(P*c8 + c9)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: c0*P^(1/3) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)**

The key features of GT are:
1. A term proportional to P^(1/3) (cube root of P)
2. A term proportional to P*exp(-c3*t)

No rational function of P can exactly reproduce P^(1/3) for all P ≥ 0. The cube root is an irrational algebraic function, while rational functions (polynomials divided by polynomials) are... rational functions. They cannot be equal for all P.

Let me check which candidates have the right basis functions.

**Candidates 1-24, 26-28, 30-31, 33-35, 38, 40-41, 44-47**: These are all rational functions of P (with exponential in t). They have the form of polynomials in P divided by linear functions of P, plus exponential terms in t. A rational function in P like P²/(P*c1+c2) = P/c1 - c2*P/(c1*(P*c1+c2)) which simplifies to polynomial + simple fraction forms. None of these can produce P^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]** for all of these.

**Candidate 8**: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+c5) + c6/(P*c4+c5) — rational in P, no P^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 25**: Has P^c5*c6 and log terms and c9*t. The P^c5 could be P^(1/3), but there's a c9*t term and log(P*c8+1) term. Setting c9=0 and c7=0 eliminates those. Then: P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2)^c3/((P*c2)^c3+1) + P*c4 + P^c5*c6. The sigmoid-like term P*c1*(Pc2)^c3/((Pc2)^c3+1) cannot be eliminated to give P*exp(-c3*t) since there's no exp(t) term at all. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 29**: P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2)^c3/((P*c2)^c3+1) + P^c4*c5 + c6*t. Has P^c4 (could be P^(1/3)), but c6*t instead of P*exp(t). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 32**: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3 + P^c4*c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*t/(P*c8+c9). Set c7=0 to kill the t/(P...) term. Then P*(c0+c3) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c4*c5*exp(c6*t). Set c6=0: P*(c0+c3) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c4*c5. Set c0+c3=0 (c3=-c0). Then: P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c5*P^c4. Set c4=1/3, c2=-c3_gt. This gives c5*P^(1/3) + c1*P*exp(-c3*t). **[MATCH]**

**Candidate 36, 37, 39, 42, 43, 48, 49, 50**: Check for P^(1/3) + P*exp(t) structure.

**Candidate 36**: P*c0+P*c1*exp(c2*t)+P*c3+P^c4*c5*exp(c6*t)+t/(P*c7+c8). Set c6=0, and the t term can't be zeroed. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 37, 43, 50**: No P^(1/3) term. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 39**: Has P^c1*c2 but also problematic terms with t and exp. **[NO MATCH]** (can't zero all unwanted terms cleanly)

**Candidate 42, 49**: Have c8*t term. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 48**: P*c0+P*c1*exp(c2*t)+P^c3*c4+c5*t/(c6*t+c7)+c8/(c6*t+c7)+t. The t terms can't all be zeroed. **[NO MATCH]**
